DOGS
§ 91.01 DEFINITIONS.
   For the purpose of this subchapter, the following definitions apply unless
the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning.
   AT LARGE. Any dog shall be deemed to be AT LARGE when it is off the property
of its owner and not under the control of a responsible person.
   DEPARTMENT OF AGRICULTURE. The Department of Agriculture of the state.
   DOG. Includes a female as well as a male DOG.
   INOCULATION AGAINST RABIES. The injection, subcutaneously or otherwise, as
approved by the Department of Agriculture of the state of canine anti-rabic
vaccine, approved by the Department of Agriculture.
   OWNER. A person having a right of property in a dog or who keeps or harbors
a dog, or who has a dog in his or her care, or who acts as its custodian, or
who knowingly permits a dog to remain on or about any premises occupied by him
or her.
   RESTRAINT. A dog is UNDER RESTRAINT within the meaning of this subchapter if
he or she is controlled by a leash, at heel beside a responsible person, or
obedient to that person’s commands, within a vehicle being driven or parked on
the streets, or within the property limits of its owner or keeper.
(Prior Code, § 3-1-1)
§ 91.02 DOGS TO BE INOCULATED AND TO HAVE NAME TAGS AFFIXED TO COLLARS.
   (A)   Each calendar year, or at such intervals as may hereafter be
promulgated by the Department of Agriculture, every owner or keeper of a dog
three months or more of age, shall cause such dog to be inoculated against
rabies. Such owner or keeper of such dog shall cause a serially numbered tag
evidencing such inoculation to be attached to a collar or harness worn by the
dog.
   (B)   Every owner or keeper of a dog, regardless of age, shall cause said
dog to wear a collar or harness and shall affix thereto a metallic or other
suitable tag inscribed with the name, address, and phone number, if any, of the
owner or keeper of the dog.
(Prior Code, § 3-1-2) Penalty, see §
91.99
§ 91.03 INOCULATION TO BE PERFORMED BY LICENSED VETERINARIAN; ISSUANCE OF
CERTIFICATE.
   The inoculation of dogs required by §
91.02(A) shall be performed by a veterinarian duly licensed to practice his or
her profession in this state. Upon performing such inoculation, such
veterinarian shall issue to the owner or keeper a certificate showing such fact
and shall also deliver to such owner or keeper a metallic or other suitable tag
to be attached to the collar or harness of such dog, which tag shall also
certify to the fact of inoculation against rabies.
(Prior Code, § 3-1-4)
§ 91.04 DURATION OF INOCULATION.
   The inoculation performed under the provisions of §
91.03 shall be effective until the expiration of the calendar year in which the
vaccination was performed or the expiration of such period of time as may be
promulgated by the Department of Agriculture.
(Prior Code, § 3-1-5)
§ 91.05 SPECIFICATIONS FOR TAG.
   The tag issued under the provisions of §
91.03 shall be in such form as shall be determined by the Department of
Agriculture.
(Prior Code, § 3-1-6)
§ 91.06 EXHIBITION OF CERTIFICATE UPON REQUEST.
   At any reasonable time upon request of any member of the Police Department,
the owner or keeper of any unmuzzled dog shall exhibit his or her certificate
issued under the provisions of §
91.03 showing the inoculation against rabies of any dog owned or controlled by
him or her.
(Prior Code, § 3-1-7)
§ 91.07 RESTRAINT OF DOGS.
   The owner or keeper of a dog shall keep the dog under restraint at all times
and shall not permit such dog to be at large, off the premises of the property
of the owner or keeper, unless the dog is under complete control as defined in
§
91.01.
(Prior Code, § 3-1-8)
§ 91.08 IMPOUNDMENT OF DOGS RUNNING AT LARGE OR UNLICENSED DOGS; CITATION OF
OWNER OR KEEPER.
   (A)   It shall be the duty of such employees and officers of the Police
Department as shall be designated for that purpose by the Chief of Police to
take up and impound in such place as may be designated and set apart for that
purpose, any dog found running at large or unlicensed in the village, contrary
to any of the provisions of this subchapter or other ordinances of the village.
   (B)   When dogs are found running at large or unlicensed and their ownership
is known to the designated employees, such dogs may be impounded at the
discretion of such employees, but the employees shall cite the owner of such
dog to answer charges for violation of this subchapter.
(Prior Code, § 3-1-9)
§ 91.09 NOTICE AND CITATION TO OWNER OR KEEPER OF IMPOUNDMENT.
   In case of impounding and where the owner or keeper of such dog is disclosed
by any tax or license tag worn by it, or is otherwise known to the officers
impounding same, the Police Department shall at once give notice by mail to
such owner or keeper, informing him or her of the impounding of his or her dog
and shall cite the owner or keeper of such dog to answer charges of violation
of this subchapter.
(Prior Code, § 3-1-11)
§ 91.10 REDEMPTION OF IMPOUNDED DOGS.
   (A)   Any dog impounded under the provisions of this code, except such as
may have bitten any person, as specified in §
91.12, shall, unless sooner redeemed, be held for the period of three days in
order to afford opportunity to the owner or keeper thereof to redeem the same.
Any such owner or keeper desiring to redeem his or her impounded dog shall pay
the sum of $5.
   (B)   In case such dog has not been inoculated against rabies for the
current year, such owner shall also advance the fee required to have such dog
inoculated by a duly licensed veterinarian as he or she shall elect, and the
poundkeeper shall forthwith cause the dog to be duly inoculated against rabies.
No dog shall be released without having been inoculated for the current
calendar year, or in accordance with the requirements of the Department of
Agriculture. Upon payment of the required charges, the dog shall thereupon be
released to the owner or keeper.
(Prior Code, § 3-1-12)
§ 91.11 DESTRUCTION OF UNREDEEMED DOGS.
   Any impounded dog which shall not be redeemed within three days shall be
humanely destroyed or otherwise disposed of by the poundkeeper.
(Prior Code, § 3-1-13)
§ 91.12 IMPOUNDMENT OF DOGS WHICH HAVE BITTEN PERSONS.
   (A)   Any dog which shall have bitten or otherwise injured any person so as
to cause an abrasion of the skin shall be immediately taken, impounded, and
kept separated from other dogs for 14 days. If, during that period, such dog
develops symptoms of illness, a veterinarian shall be called to diagnose its
condition. If the symptoms disclosed are such as to indicate the presence of
rabies, such dog shall be destroyed in such a manner, however, as to preserve
intact the head, which shall thereupon be detached and immediately sent to the
diagnostic laboratory of the Department of Agriculture. In case such dog cannot
be safely taken up and impounded, it may be shot, care being taken to preserve
the head intact, which shall thereupon be immediately detached and be delivered
to the diagnostic laboratory of the Department of Agriculture.
   (B)   If, at the expiration of the period of 14 days, no symptoms of rabies
have developed in such dog so impounded, the same may be redeemed by the owner
upon payment of the redemption fees and charges specified by §
91.10; provided, however, that in case any dog so impounded for biting a person
shall have previously bitten any person, such dog shall be humanely destroyed
by the poundkeeper. After having been notified that his or her dog has bitten
or otherwise injured any person, the owner or keeper thereof shall not, under
any circumstances, permit such animal to be at large unless securely muzzled.
(Prior Code, § 3-1-14) Penalty, see §
91.99
§ 91.13 VILLAGE MAY PROVIDE POUND.
   The village may designate a suitable place for the impounding of dogs.
(Prior Code, § 3-1-15)
§ 91.14 DISPOSITION OF DOGS DEEMED NUISANCES.
   Any dog which may in any manner continually disturb the quiet of any
person’s or neighborhood’s property, or shall destroy in any manner, injure any
animal, plant, shrub, or other property not on the premises of its owner or
keeper, is hereby declared to be a nuisance, and such dog shall be taken up and
impounded and may be redeemed or disposed of in the manner provided for under §
91.11.
(Prior Code, § 3-1-16)
§ 91.15 DUTIES OF CHIEF OF POLICE AND MANAGER OF ANIMAL SHELTER RELATIVE TO
SUBCHAPTER.
   Except as to the regulations concerning inoculation against rabies, the
Chief of Police is charged with the duty of enforcing the provisions of this
subchapter.
(Prior Code, § 3-1-17)
§ 91.16 DUTIES OF VILLAGE CLERK.
   It shall be the duty of the Village Clerk to determine that all fees herein
provided or otherwise provided by law to be paid are properly accounted for to
the Village Treasurer.
(Prior Code, § 3-1-18)
§ 91.17 UNKNOWN OWNER; POSTING NOTICE.
   When any animal is impounded and its owner is unknown, there shall be placed
at the Village Hall by the dog catcher a notice describing the said animal and
where it is located.
(Prior Code, § 3-1-19)
§ 91.18 DOG CATCHER.
   The Mayor may appoint the dog catcher by and with the consent of the Village
Board. The salary shall be established in the annual appropriation ordinance.
(Prior Code, § 3-1-20)
ANIMALS
§ 91.30 DEFINITIONS.
   For the purpose of this subchapter, the following definitions apply unless
the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning.
   ANIMAL CONTROL OFFICER. Any person hired by the village to perform the
duties assigned to that person by the Village Animal Control Act.
   BOARD. The Village Board of Trustees.
   DANGEROUS DOG. Any individual dog which, when either unmuzzled, unleashed,
or unattended by its owner or a member of its owner’s family, in a vicious or
terrorizing manner, approaches any person in an apparent attitude of attack
upon streets, sidewalks, or any public grounds or places.
   DOG. All members of the family canidae.
   LEASH. A cord, rope, strap, chain, or frame which shall be securely fastened
to the collar or harness of a dog or other animal and shall be of sufficient
strength to keep such dog or other under control.
   OWNER. Any person having a right of property in a dog, cat, or other animal,
or who has a dog or other animal in his or her care, or acts as the custodian,
or who knowingly permits a dog or other domestic animal to remain on or about
any premises occupied by him or her.
   STRAY DOG. Any dog not on the premises of the dog’s owners or under control
by leash, or identification by collar or tags.
   VICIOUS DOG. 
      (1)   An individual dog that, when unprovoked, inflicts bites or attacks
a human being or other animal, either on public or private property.
      (2)   Any individual dog with a known propensity, tendency, or
disposition to attack without provocation, to cause injury or to otherwise
endanger the safety of human beings or domestic animals.
      (3)   Any individual dog that has a trait or characteristic and a
generally known reputation for viciousness, dangerousness, or unprovoked upon
human beings or other animals, unless handled in a particular manner or with
special equipment.
      (4)   Any individual dog which attacks a human being or domestic animal
without provocation.
      (5)   Any individual dog which has been found to a be a dangerous dog
upon three separate occasions.
      (6)   No dog shall be deemed VICIOUS if it bites, attacks, or menaces a
trespasser on the property of its owner or harms or menaces anyone who has
tormented or abused it or is a professionally trained dog for law enforcement
or guard duties. VICIOUS DOGS shall not be classified in a manner that is
specific as to breed.
   VETERINARIAN. A licensed veterinarian in the state and appointed pursuant to
this subchapter.
(Prior Code, § 4-1-1)
§ 91.31 PERSONNEL.
   The Chairperson of the Village Board shall appoint, with the advice and
consent of the Board, an Animal Control Officer whose salary and expenses shall
be set annually by the Board and incorporated in the annual budget. Said Animal
Control Officer may be removed by the Board for cause or may be reassigned at
the discretion of the Board.
(Prior Code, § 4-1-2)
§ 91.32 DUTIES OF THE ANIMAL CONTROL OFFICER.
   (A)   It shall be the duty of the Animal Control Officer to control and
prevent the spread of rabies through education, rabies inoculation, stray dog,
and animal control, impoundment, quarantine, and any other means deemed
necessary.
   (B)   The Animal Control Officer shall have the following duties:
      (1)   Administer and implement the animal control program in the village;
      (2)   Make such reports as are required by the Director of the State
Department of Agriculture and the Village Board;
      (3)   To answer to the Village Board whenever requested so to do
concerning the operation of the village’s animal control program; and
      (4)   Such other duties as are delineated in a job description formulated
and approved by the Village Board of Trustees.
(Prior Code, § 4-1-3)
§ 91.33 POWERS OF THE VILLAGE BOARD.
   The Village Board, by virtue of this subchapter, shall have the following
authority and/or powers:
   (A)   To draft written rules and regulations for the operation of the
Village Board’s animal control program;
   (B)   To prepare an annual budget for the operation of the village animal
control program; and
   (C)   To approve all expenditures under the animal control program.
(Prior Code, § 4-1-4)
§ 91.34 POLICE POWERS.
   (A)   The Animal Control Officer, for the purpose of enforcing the village
animal control program, shall have the power and authority of police officers
in the village and/or peace officers in the village, including, but not limited
to, the power and authority to issue and serve citations, summonses, and
orders, as well as serving and executing and serving all warrants and processes
issued by any Circuit Court.
   (B)   Said Animal Control Officer shall be authorized to carry mace, a
tranquilizer gun, and such other weapons as authorized by the Board, within its
discretion, said weapons to be carried in the vehicle of the officer and used
only in case of an emergency.
(Prior Code, § 4-1-5)
§ 91.35 ANIMAL BITE.
   (A)   Any individual having knowledge that a person has been bitten by a dog
or other animal, and who fails to report such incident to the Animal Control
Officer, is in violation of this subchapter. It shall be the duty of any person
conducting or operating a medical facility, or any physician, nurse, or other
medical personnel to report to the local law enforcement agency or to the
Animal Control Officer when a person is treated for any injury resulting from
an animal bite.
   (B)   It shall then be the duty of any and all law enforcement personnel to
report to the Animal Control Officer any reports which are received concerning
a person being bitten by said animal.
   (C)   When the Animal Control Officer receives information that a person
other than a family member has been bitten by a dog or other animal, said
officer or his or her authorized representative shall have such dog or other
animal quarantined with a licensed veterinarian, for a period of ten days. When
a dog or other animal is quarantined for biting a person, the following steps
shall occur.
      (1)   The Animal Control Officer or his or her authorized representative
shall attempt to determine from the owner of the dog, or other animal to be
quarantined, at which veterinarian’s office said owner would prefer to have
their dog or animal quarantined. If designation of such a veterinarian is
impossible, or quarantine at the designated veterinarian is impossible,
veterinarians who maintain quarantine facilities in the region shall be used as
directed by the Village Board.
      (2)   The Animal Control Officer or his or her authorized representative
shall, in writing, notify the owner of the dog or other animal to be
quarantined, if the owner is known that he or she is responsible for all
quarantine costs and if the dog, or other animal, is not retrieved in ten days
with all costs being paid at that time, the animal shall be humanely destroyed,
or may be adopted upon inoculation and payment of all realized costs and
expenses of the village.
      (3)   The veterinarian observing the quarantined dog, or other animal
shall immediately report the clinical condition of the animal to the Animal
Control Officer, with confirmation in writing, within 24 hours, giving the
owner’s name, address, date of confinement, breed, description, age, and sex of
such dog or other animal on forms approved by the State Department of
Agriculture.
      (4)   At the end of said quarantine period, the veterinarian observing
the quarantined dog, or other animal, shall submit a written report to the
Animal Control Officer, advising him or her of the final disposition of the
animal on forms approved by the State Department of Agriculture.
(Prior Code, § 4-1-6) Penalty, see §
91.99
§ 91.36 REGISTRATION OF FORMS AND TAG FEES.
   (A)   The Animal Control Officer shall provide licensed veterinarians with
rabies inoculation certificates in a form approved by the Village Board, which
shall be signed by the veterinarian administering the rabies inoculation
vaccine. The original of said certificate shall be issued to the owner of the
dog which has been inoculated and a copy of the certificate shall be returned
to the Animal Control Officer or his or her designated representative as soon
as practicable, preferably monthly.
   (B)   The Village Board shall provide annual rabies inoculation tags at a
set fee as determined by the Village Board. Rabies inoculation tags shall be in
a form and color prescribed by the State Department of Agriculture.
   (C)   All registration fees collected shall be remitted to the Village
Treasurer, who shall place such monies in an Animal Control Fund, which shall
be established for the purpose of paying costs of the animal control program.
These funds shall be used for paying the cost of stray dog control,
impoundment, education on animal control, rabies, and other costs incurred in
carrying out the provisions of this subchapter.
(Prior Code, § 4-1-7)
§ 91.37 INOCULATION REQUIREMENTS.
   Every owner of a dog or cat four months of age or older shall cause such dog
or cat to be inoculated against tables by a licensed veterinarian annually or
every three years, depending on the type of vaccine used, June 30 of the
current year being the deadline for such inoculation.
(Prior Code, § 4-1-8)
§ 91.38 COLLAR AND IDENTIFICATION REQUIREMENTS.
   Every owner of a dog four months of age or older shall cause a current,
valid rabies inoculation tag to be attached to a collar or harness and worn by
the dog to which the tag was issued at all times. Every owner of a dog under
four months of age shall have a tag specifying the owner’s name, address, and
telephone number attached to a collar or harness, which shall be worn by the
dog at all times.
(Prior Code, § 4-1-9) Penalty, see §
91.99
§ 91.39 CONTROL BY OWNER.
   Every owner of a dog shall keep such dog from leaving the premises occupied
by said owner unless the dog is accompanied or supervised by its owner or on a
leash.
(Prior Code, § 4-1-10) Penalty, see §
91.99
§ 91.40 NUISANCE ANIMALS.
   Any dog or other animal which howls, barks, or utters any other annoying and
disturbing sound which can be heard beyond the boundary or the premises of its
owner, with such volume and frequency so as to unreasonably disturb any
resident of the village is hereby declared to be a public nuisance and is
hereby declared to be subject to the control, regulation, impoundment, and
abatement as provided herein and as provided by the laws of the state.
(Prior Code, § 4-1-11) Penalty, see §
91.99
§ 91.41 VICIOUS AND DANGEROUS DOGS.
   (A)   It shall be unlawful for any person to keep or maintain any dog which
has been found to be a vicious dog unless such dog is at all times kept in an
enclosure, which is a fence or structure of at least six feet in height,
forming or causing an enclosure, suitable to prevent the entry of young
children, and suitable to confine a vicious dog in conduction with other
measures which may be taken by the owner or keeper, such as tethering of a
vicious dog within the enclosure.
   (B)   The only times that a vicious dog may be allowed out of the enclosure
are:
      (1)   If it is necessary for the owner or keeper to obtain veterinary
care for the dog; or
      (2)   To comply with the order of a court of competent jurisdiction,
provided that the dog is securely muzzled and restrained with a chain having a
tensile strength of 300 pounds and not exceeding three feet in length, and
shall be under the direct control and supervision of the owner or keeper of the
dog.
   (C)   Any dog which has been found to be a vicious dog and which is not
confined to an enclosure shall be impounded by the Administrator, Animal
Control Officer, or the law enforcement authority having jurisdiction in such
area, and shall be turned over to a licensed veterinarian for destruction by
lethal injection.
   (D)   No owner or keeper of a vicious dog shall sell or give away the dog.
(Prior Code, § 4-1-12) Penalty, see §
91.99
§ 91.42 IMPOUNDMENT.
   The Animal Control Officer shall, and any peace officer may, apprehend and
impound the following dogs and/or other domestic animals:
   (A)   Dogs or other animals which have bitten a person;
   (B)   Dogs of four months of age or older which have not been inoculated
against rabies by a licensed veterinarian. Dogs who are four months of age or
older and who are confined on the owner’s premises in keeping with the
provisions of this subchapter are exempt;
   (C)   Dogs four months of age of older, not on the premises of their owner,
and which do not have a current, valid rabies inoculation tag attached to their
collar or harness;
   (D)   Dogs under four months of age not on the premises of their owner and
which do not have an identification tag specifying the owner’s name, address,
and telephone number attached to their collar or harness; and
   (E)   Dogs wearing a current valid rabies inoculation tag or identification
tag which are not on the premises occupied by the dog’s owner and are not
accompanied or supervised by the owner and are not on a leash when a complaint
has been received by the Animal Control Officer.
(Prior Code, § 4-1-13)
§ 91.43 NOTICE OF IMPOUNDMENT.
   (A)   When a dog or cat whose owner is known is impounded, notice shall be
immediately given to the owner by the Animal Control Officer or his or her
authorized representative. Notice shall be mailed to the owner at the last
known mailing address, by regular mail, postage prepaid. An affidavit or
testimony of the Animal Control Officer or his or her authorized representative
who mails the notice shall be prima facie evidence of the receipt of such
notice by the owner.
   (B)   In the case of dogs, cats, or other animals impounded pursuant to §
91.42, or if the dog or other animal is not redeemed within seven days from the
date the notice was mailed, or the dog or other animal impounded, if the owner
is unknown, the impounded dog or other animal shall be humanely dispatched, or
offered for adoption, in accordance with this subchapter or the laws that exist
or may hereinafter exist.
(Prior Code, § 4-1-14)
§ 91.44 REDEMPTION.
   When the owner of any dog or other animal impounded pursuant to §
91.42 desire to redeem the same, the following procedure shall be followed.
   (A)   At the time of impoundment, the Animal Control Officer shall prepare
an impoundment form to be approved and supplied by the Village Board,
indicating the amount of fine and costs, if imposed, as well as the total
amount of board and impoundment expenses which are due and owing the village.
   (B)   The impounding authority shall place on the impounding form a charge
of $5 per day for each day or part thereof when the dog or other animal was
impounded, plus a pickup fee in the amount of $25.
   (C)   Prior to release, the animal control warden shall provide an up-to-
date copy of the impoundment form to the Village Treasurer, indicating the
amounts owed. Upon full payment being received from the owner, a receipt or
other form indicating said payment shall be provided to the owner, who shall
then present said document to the Animal Control Officer prior to the release
of his or her dog.
   (D)   The owner shall then present to the Animal Control Officer a current
rabies inoculation certificate and a receipt from the Village Treasurer
confirming that the total amount due, as indicated by the impoundment form, has
been paid in full. If no current rabies certificate is available, notice is to
be issued to the owner that the animal must be inoculated within five days.
   (E)   Animals may only be redeemed during normal business hours, Monday
through Friday, or as directed by the Animal Control Officer, with the advice
and consent of the Village Board, and all fees, excluding fines and costs,
which are due the County Circuit Clerk, shall be paid at the Village Hall
between the hours of 8:00 a.m. and 4:00 p.m., Monday through Friday, excluding
recognized county holidays.
(Prior Code, § 4-1-15)
§ 91.45 COLLECTION OF FUNDS.
   Any and all amounts collected by the Village Clerk pursuant to this section
and subchapter shall be placed in a separate account to be known as the Animal
Control Fund, and shall be used in paying the costs of operating the animal
control program.
(Prior Code, § 4-1-16)
§ 91.46 PREVENTION OF SPREAD OF RABIES.
   (A)   Whenever a case of rabies has occurred in a locality, or when the
proper officials of a government unit are apprehensive of the spread of rabies,
the Village Board may order the following:
      (1)   All dogs or other animals in the locality shall be:
         (a)   Kept confined within an enclosure; or
         (b)   Kept muzzled and restrained by a leash.
      (2)   All owners or keepers of dogs or other animals take prophylactic
measures it deems necessary to prevent the spread of rabies; and
      (3)   Other measures as may be necessary to prevent the spread of rabies.
   (B)   The Village Board may determine the area of the locality in which, and
the period of time during which, such orders shall be effective.
(Prior Code, § 4-1-17)
§ 91.47 APPREHENSION AND INVESTIGATION.
   (A)   For the purposes of carrying out the provisions of this subchapter,
the Animal Control Officer, or his or her authorized representative, or any
peace officer, may enter onto private property as follows:
      (1)   To apprehend a dog or other animal thought to be infected with
rabies;
      (2)   To apprehend a straying dog or other animal; or
      (3)   To apprehend a dog or other animal who has bitten any person.
   (B)   At the request of the owner or occupier of private property, the
Animal Control Officer or his or her authorized representative may enter onto
such property to apprehend any dog, whether or not said dog is wearing a rabies
inoculation tag or identification tag.
(Prior Code, § 4-1-18)
§ 91.48 CITATIONS.
   Animal Control Officers and all peace officers in the village may issue
citations to animal owners for violations of this subchapter in lieu of
impounding the animal. When such citation is issued, and appearance date of not
less than ten days and not more than 45 days shall be entered by the officer,
on the citation itself. The owner of the animal may plead guilty to the offense
charged in the citation prior the scheduled appearance date by so indicating on
the citation and paying a fine as described in §
91.99.
(Prior Code, § 4-1-19) (Ord. 2019-1, passed 6-4-2018)
§ 91.49 DUMPING OF ANIMALS.
   No person shall cause any animal to be dumped or abandoned in any
incorporated or unincorporated area of the village.
(Prior Code, § 4-1-20) Penalty, see §
91.99
§ 91.99 PENALTY.
   (A)   Any person violating any provision of this chapter for which no
specific penalty is prescribed shall be subject to §
10.99 of this code of ordinances.
   (B)   (1)   The owner of the animal cited as described in §
91.48 may plead guilty to the offense charged in the citation prior to the
scheduled appearance date by so indicating on the citation and paying a fine of
$50 for first citation, plus any court costs, to the County Circuit Clerk.
      (2)   A second violation by the same animal shall be punishable by a fine
of $200, plus costs and shall require court appearances. Subsequent repeated
offenses could be cited up to $400, plus costs and court fees.
(Prior Code, § 4-1-19)
   (C)   Any person who is convicted of such offense as described in §
91.49 shall be guilty of a petty offense and shall be fined not less than $100
nor more than $500, with each violation being considered a separate offense.
(Prior Code, § 4-1-20)
   (D)   Any person violating any provision of §§
91.30 to 91.49, except as stated in divisions (B) and (C) above, or any person
who counterfeits or forges any rabies inoculation certificate, shall be guilty
of a petty offense and, upon conviction thereto, shall be fined in an amount of
not less than $25 and not more than $200.
(Prior Code, § 4-1-21)
(Ord. 2019-1, passed 6-4-2018)
CHAPTER 92: FIRE PREVENTION
Section
General Provisions
   
92.01   Fire Prevention Code
Open Burning
   
92.15   Permitted and prohibited burn items
   
92.16   Acceptable conditions for burning
   
92.17   Recreational fires
   
92.18   Abatement and jurisdiction
 
   
92.99   Penalty
GENERAL PROVISIONS
§ 92.01 FIRE PREVENTION CODE.
   The Fire Prevention Code recommended by the American Insurance Association,
being particularly the 1965 Edition, is hereby adopted by reference, pursuant
to authority of 24 Ill. Rev. Stat. 10-3 and 1241 to 1247, inclusive; provided,
that if any of the provisions of the Fire Prevention Code are in conflict with
state law or any ordinance of the village, the state law or such ordinance
shall prevail. At least three copies of such Fire Prevention Code will be found
on file in the office of the Village Clerk and are available for public use,
inspection, and examination.
(Prior Code, § 30-4-1) Penalty, see §
92.99
OPEN BURNING
§ 92.15 PERMITTED AND PROHIBITED BURN ITEMS.
   (A)   Only natural yard waste such as leaves, lawn clippings, small limbs,
and shrub clipping resulting from routine private resident lawn maintenance are
allowed to be burned and must be burned on the premises on which such yard
waste is generated or fallen upon. Any tree limbs, sticks, branches, or debris
accumulated by residents in private yards within the village limits can be
dropped off at the village’s free dump site on Old Marion Road. Residents must
first check in with the Village Hall and sign for the key.
   (B)   Burning of domicile waste (garbage) or agricultural waste is
prohibited.
   (C)   There will be no burning of building materials, including sawn lumber.
   (D)   Burning of any combustible materials, such as roofing, mattresses,
carpet, or any items which may explode are prohibited.
   (E)   Commercial burning of any kind is prohibited. Any commercial burn will
be extinguished and billed under the illegal burns section of the Village Fire
Department Billing Ordinance.
(Ord. 2024-8, passed 10-2-2023) Penalty, see §
92.99
§ 92.16 ACCEPTABLE CONDITIONS FOR BURNING.
   (A)   Private residents can perform legal burns on their property within the
village limits between the hours of 8:00 a.m. and 8:00 p.m.
      (1)   If a private resident plans to perform a controlled legal burn, he
or she must first contact one of the following entities prior to the burn:
         (a)   Village Hall 618-995-2157 (Monday through Friday, 8:00 a.m. to
4:00 p.m.); or
         (b)   County Sheriff Department 618-658-8284.
      (2)   Provide the following information:
         (a)   Location of the proposed burn;
         (b)   Items being burned;
         (c)   Contact person with phone number; and
         (d)   Approximate hours of the burn.
   (B)   It is illegal to burn within two feet of the margin of any cement,
bituminous, or other hard surfaced paved street, highway, or sidewalk within,
or partly within the village limits. No burning shall occur on a village
street.
   (C)   Any burning is prohibited if it creates a visibility hazard on a
roadway, railroad, or airfield.
   (D)   No burning may be conducted within 20 feet of a residence or building.
   (E)   Burning may be in barrels or on the ground but must be attended at all
times.
   (F)   No one shall burn at any time the wind velocity, to a prudent person,
is such as to cause the burning to be a hazard to life or property. A violation
of this division (F) shall be presumed if, but not limited to, burning leaves
are blown from the immediate area in which it is being burned or atmospheric
conditions allow contaminants to be blown onto the property of another, causing
damage to real property or creating a nuisance to another person(s).
   (G)   Burning must be conducted when conditions will readily dissipate
contaminants.
(Ord. 2024-8, passed 10-2-2023) Penalty, see §
92.99
§ 92.17 RECREATIONAL FIRES.
   (A)   RECREATIONAL FIRES shall consist of the burning of fuels for a
legitimate campfire, recreation, and cooking purposes, or in a domestic
fireplace, in an area where such burning is consistent with other laws,
provided that no garbage shall be burned in such case.
   (B)   The fire shall be conducted in a cleared open area of no less than a
20-foot radius.
   (C)   The fire shall occur in an appliance designed for such burning, a burn
pit, or an area surrounded by noncombustible material.
   (D)   No fires shall be allowed when winds are such as to cause a hazard to
life or property.
(Ord. 2024-8, passed 10-2-2023) Penalty, see §
92.99
§ 92.18 ABATEMENT AND JURISDICTION.
   (A)   The Village Fire Department will extinguish all illegal fires/burns.
   (B)   This subchapter applies to village limits only.
(Ord. 2024-8, passed 10-2-2023)
§ 92.99 PENALTY.
   (A)   Any person violating any provision of this chapter for which no
specific penalty is prescribed shall be subject to §
10.99 of this code of ordinances.
   (B)   Whoever violates any of the provisions of the Fire Prevention Code
adopted by §
92.01, or any of the provisions of the code shall, upon conviction therefor, be
punished by a fine not less than $3, nor more than $200. Each day any
violations of any provisions of such Fire Prevention Code or the provisions of
§
92.01 shall continue shall constitute a separate offense.
(Prior Code, § 30-4-2)
   (C)   Any village resident or an individual person (non-commercial) within
the village limits in violation of §§
92.15 to
92.18 shall be fined on the schedule below:
      (1)   Occurrence #1: written warning;
      (2)   Occurrence #2: fine of $125;
      (3)   Occurrence #3: fine of $250;
      (4)   Occurrence #4: fine of $500;
      (5)   Occurrence #5: fine of $1,000; and
      (6)   Occurrence #6 and beyond will result in a meeting with the Public
Safety Committee and a fine starting at $2,000.
(Ord. 2024-8, passed 10-2-2023)
CHAPTER 93: FAIR HOUSING
Section
   
93.01   Declaration of policy
   
93.02   Definitions
   
93.03   Prohibited acts
 
   
93.99   Penalty
§ 93.01 DECLARATION OF POLICY.
   (A)   In furthering the policy of the state as expressed in its Constitution
and other laws, in order that the safety and general welfare, peace, and health
of all the inhabitants of the village may be ensured, it is hereby declared the
policy of the village to assure equal opportunity to all residents, regardless
of race, color, religion, national origin or ancestry, sex, creed, or physical
disability to live in decent, sanitary, healthful, standard living quarters.
   (B)   It is the policy of the village that no owner, lessee, sub-lessee,
assignee, managing agent, or other person, firm, or corporation having the
right to sell, rent, lease, or otherwise control any housing accommodation and/
or real property within the village, or any agent of these shall refuse to
sell, rent, lease, or otherwise deny to or withhold from any person or group of
persons such housing accommodations and/or real property because of race,
color, religion, national origin or ancestry, sex, creed, or disability in the
conditions, terms, privileges of the sale, rental, or lease of any housing
accommodation and/or real property or in the furnishing of facilities and/or
services in connection therewith.
   (C)   Relocation shall be carried out in a manner that will promote maximum
choice within the community’s total housing supply, lessen racial, ethnic, and
economic concentrations, and facilitate desegregation and racially inclusive
patterns of occupancy and use of public and private facilities.
(Ord. 2005-2, passed 11-1-2004) Penalty, see §
93.99
§ 93.02 DEFINITIONS.
   For the purpose of this chapter, the following definitions apply unless the
context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning.
   DECENT, SANITARY, HEALTHFUL STANDARD LIVING QUARTERS. Housing which is in
sound, clean, and weather-tight condition in conformance with applicable local,
state, and national codes.
   DISCRIMINATE or DISCRIMINATION. Any difference expressed in any way toward a
person or persons in the terms of the sale, exchange, lease, rental, or
financing for housing accommodation and/or real property in regard to such
sale, exchange, rental, lease, or finance because of race, color, religion,
national origin or ancestry, sex, creed, or disability of such person.
   FINANCIAL INSTITUTION. Any person, institution, or business entity of any
kind which loans money to persons and receives as security for said loans a
secured interest of any kind in the real property of the borrower.
   HOUSING ACCOMMODATION. Includes any building, structure, or portion thereof
which is used or occupied, maintained, arranged, or designed to be used or
occupied as a home, residence, or sleeping place of one or more human beings,
or any real estate so used, designed, or intended for such use.
   OWNER. Any person/persons who hold legal or equitable title to, or own any
beneficial interest in any real property or who hold legal or equitable title
to shares of, or hold any beneficial interest in any real estate cooperative
which owns any real property and/or housing accommodations.
   REAL ESTATE BROKER. Any person, partnership, association, corporation, and/
or agent thereof who, for a fee or other valuable consideration, offers, sells,
purchases, exchanges, or rents, or negotiates for the sale, purchase, exchange,
or rental of a housing accommodation and/or real property of another, or
collects rental for the use of housing accommodation and/or real property of
another.
   REAL PROPERTY. Any real estate, vacant land, building, structure, or housing
accommodations within the corporate limits of the village.
(Ord. 2005-2, passed 11-1-2004)
§ 93.03 PROHIBITED ACTS.
   (A)   It shall be unlawful for any owner of real estate, lessee, sub-lessee,
real estate broker, or salesperson, financial institution, or employee of the
financial institution, advertiser, or agent of any or all of the foregoing, to
discriminate against any person or persons because of his, her, or their race,
color, religion, national origin or ancestry, sex, creed, or disability with
regard to the sale, exchange, or rental, or any dealing concerning any housing
accommodation and/or real property.
   (B)   In addition to division (A) above, it shall also be unlawful for any
real estate broker or employee thereof, owner, or other person, or financial
institution dealing with housing or real property in the village:
      (1)   To discriminate against any person in the availability of or the
price, terms, conditions, or privileges of any kind relating to the sale,
rental, lease, or occupancy of any housing accommodation or real property in
the village or in furnishing of any facilities or services in connection
therewith;
      (2)   To publish or circulate, or cause to be published or circulated,
any notice, statement, or advertisement, or to announce a policy, or to use any
form of application for the purchase, lease, rental, or financing of real
property, or to make any record of inquiry in connection with the prospective
purchase, rental, or lease of such real estate, which expresses directly or
indirectly any discrimination as to race, color, religion, national origin or
ancestry, sex, creed, or disability of any person;
      (3)   To discriminate in connection with lending money, guaranteeing
loans, accepting mortgages, or otherwise obtaining or making available funds
for the purchase, acquisition, construction, rehabilitation, repair, or
maintenance of any housing accommodation and/or real property;
      (4)   To solicit for sale, lease, or listing for the sale or lease of any
housing accommodation and/or real property on the grounds of loss of value
because of the present or prospective entry into any neighborhood of any person
or persons of any particular race, color, religion, national origin or
ancestry, sex, creed, or disability;
      (5)   To distribute, or cause to be distributed, written material or
statements designed to induce any owner or any housing accommodation and/or
real property to sell or lease his or her property because of any present or
prospective change in the race, color, religion, national origin or ancestry,
sex, creed, or disability of persons in the neighborhood;
      (6)   To make any misrepresentations concerning the listing for sale, or
the anticipated listing for sale, or the sale of any housing accommodation and/
or real property for the purpose of inducing or attempting to induce the sale
or listing for sale of any housing accommodation and/or real property by
representing that the presence or anticipated presence of persons of any
particular race, color, religion, national origin or ancestry, sex, creed, or
disability in the area will or may result in the lowering of property values in
the block, neighborhood, or area in which the property is located;
      (7)   For an owner to solicit any real estate broker to sell, rent, or
otherwise deal with such owner’s housing accommodations and/or real property
with any limitation on its sale based on race, color, religion, national origin
or ancestry, sex, creed, or disability; or
      (8)   For an owner to refuse to sell, rent, or otherwise deal with any
housing accommodation and/or real property because of race, color, religion,
national origin or ancestry, sex, creed, or disability of the proposed buyer or
tenant.
(Ord. 2005-2, passed 11-1-2004) Penalty, see §
93.99
§ 93.99 PENALTY.
   Any person convicted of violating any of the provisions of this chapter
shall be punished by a fine of not less than $100 nor more than $1,500. Each
day a violation continues shall constitute a separate violation. This section
shall in no way abrogate or impair the right of the village to specifically
enforce, by any legal means, any of the provisions of this chapter.
(Ord. 2005-2, passed 11-1-2004)
CHAPTER 94: PARKS AND RECREATION
Section
   
94.01   Animals in parks
   
94.02   Horses on streets
   
94.03   Horses attended to
§ 94.01 ANIMALS IN PARKS.
   It shall be unlawful to ride or lead a horse or pony on sidewalks, public
playgrounds, or public parks in the village at all times.
(Prior Code, § 28-1-1) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 94.02 HORSES ON STREETS.
   Riding or leading a horse or pony is permitted from sunrise to sunset on the
streets subject to the provisions of Title VII applicable to the driver of a
vehicle.
(Prior Code, § 28-1-2) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 94.03 HORSES ATTENDED TO.
   Horses or ponies will be attended at all times as to not cause danger or
harm to any person and/or property.
(Prior Code, § 28-1-3) Penalty, see §
10.99
TITLE XI: BUSINESS REGULATIONS
   Chapter

CHAPTER 110: CONTROLLED SUBSTANCES
Section
Alcohol
   
110.01   Liquor unlawful in village

ALCOHOL
§ 110.01 LIQUOR UNLAWFUL IN VILLAGE.
   It shall be unlawful to sell, offer for sale, barter, or exchange any
intoxicating beverage in the village. It shall be unlawful to keep in the
village, for the purpose of selling the same or offering the same for sale, any
intoxicating beverage.
(Prior Code, § 21-1-1) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 110.02 MANUFACTURING UNLAWFUL.
   It shall be unlawful to bottle, manufacture, distill, or prepare for sale in
any way any intoxicating beverage within the village.
(Prior Code, § 21-1-2) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 110.03 DEFINITION.
   For the purpose of this subchapter, the following definition applies unless
the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning.
   INTOXICATING BEVERAGE. Any liquid intended for human consumption containing
more than 0.5% by volume of alcohol.
(Prior Code, § 21-1-3)
§ 110.04 SALE BY CLUB OR GIVEN TO PUBLIC.
   It shall be unlawful to serve or give any intoxicating beverage in any club,
whether or not such beverage is offered, sold, or given to the public or only
to the members of the club.
(Prior Code, § 21-1-4) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 110.05 MEDICAL TREATMENT.
   The provisions of this subchapter shall not be construed to prevent the sale
by a licensed pharmacist of any intoxicating beverage on the prescription of a
licensed physician for medical treatment.
(Prior Code, § 21-1-5)
CANNABIS
§ 110.20 RECITALS.
   The facts and statements contained in the preamble to the ordinance from
which this subchapter is derived are found to be true and correct and are
hereby adopted as part of this subchapter.
(Ord. 2020-08, passed 1-6-2020)
§ 110.21 DEFINITIONS.
   For the purpose of this subchapter, the following definitions apply unless
the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning.
   ADULT-USE CANNABIS BUSINESS ESTABLISHMENT. A cultivation center, craft
grower, processing organization, infuser organization, dispensing organization,
or transporting organization.
   ADULT-USE CANNABIS CRAFT GROWER. A facility operated by an organization or
business that is licensed by the State Department of Agriculture to cultivate,
dry, cure, and package cannabis and perform other necessary activities to make
cannabis available for sale at a dispensing organization or use at a processing
organization, per the Cannabis Regulation and Tax Act (Pub. Act 101-0027), as
it may be amended from time to time, and regulations promulgated thereunder.
   ADULT-USE CANNABIS CULTIVATION CENTER. A facility operated by an
organization or business that is licensed by the State Department of
Agriculture to cultivate, process, transport, and perform necessary activities
to provide cannabis and cannabis-infused products to licensed cannabis business
establishments, per the Cannabis Regulation and Tax Act (Pub. Act 101-0027), as
it may be amended from time to time, and regulations promulgated thereunder.
   ADULT-USE CANNABIS DISPENSING ORGANIZATION. A facility operated by an
organization or business that is licensed by the State Department of Financial
and Professional Regulation to acquire cannabis from licensed cannabis
establishments for the purpose of selling or dispensing cannabis, cannabis-
infused products, cannabis seeds, paraphernalia, or related supplies to
purchasers or to qualified registered medical cannabis patients and caregivers,
per the Cannabis Regulation and Tax Act (Pub. Act 101-0027), as it may be
amended from time to time, and regulations promulgated thereunder.
   ADULT-USE CANNABIS INFUSER ORGANIZATION OR INFUSER. A facility operated by
an organization or business that is licensed by the State Department of
Agriculture to directly incorporate cannabis or cannabis concentrate into a
product formulation to produce a cannabis-infused product, per the Cannabis
Regulation and Tax Act (Pub. Act 101-0027), as it may be amended from time to
time, and regulations promulgated thereunder.
   ADULT-USE CANNABIS PROCESSING ORGANIZATION OR PROCESSOR. A facility operated
by an organization or business that is licensed by the State Department of
Agriculture to either extract constituent chemicals or compounds to produce
cannabis concentrate or incorporate cannabis or cannabis concentrate into a
product formulation to produce a cannabis product, per the Cannabis Regulation
and Tax Act (Pub. Act 101-0027), as it may be amended from time to time, and
regulations promulgated thereunder.
   ADULT-USE CANNABIS TRANSPORTING ORGANIZATION OR TRANSPORTER. An organization
or business that is licensed by the State Department of Agriculture to
transport cannabis on behalf of a cannabis business establishment or a
community college licensed under the Community College Cannabis Vocational
Training Pilot Program, per the Cannabis Regulation and Tax Act (Pub. Act 101-
0027), as it may be amended from time to time, and regulations promulgated
thereunder.
   PERSON. Any person, firm, corporation, association, club, society, or other
organization, including any owner, manager, proprietor, employee, volunteer, or
agent.
(Ord. 2020-08, passed 1-6-2020)
§ 110.22 CANNABIS BUSINESS ESTABLISHMENTS PROHIBITED.
   The following adult-use cannabis business establishments are prohibited in
the village. No person shall locate, operate, own, suffer, allow to be
operated, or aid, abet, or assist in the operation within the village of any of
the following:
   (A)   Adult-use cannabis craft grower;
   (B)   Adult-use cannabis cultivation center;
   (C)   Adult-use cannabis dispensing organization;
   (D)   Adult-use cannabis infuser organization or infuser;
   (E)   Adult-use cannabis processing organization or processor; or
   (F)   Adult-use cannabis transporting organization or transporter.
(Ord. 2020-08, passed 1-6-2020) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 110.23 PUBLIC NUISANCE DECLARED.
   Operation of any prohibited cannabis business establishment within the
village in violation of the provisions of this subchapter is hereby declared a
public nuisance and shall be abated pursuant to all available remedies.
(Ord. 2020-08, passed 1-6-2020)
§ 110.24 VIOLATIONS.
   Violations of this subchapter may be enforced in accordance with the
provisions established herein.
(Ord. 2020-08, passed 1-6-2020)
CHAPTER 111: GAMBLING
Section
Video Gambling
   
111.01   Recitals
   
111.02   Permitted facilities
   
111.03   Licenses and fees
 
   
111.99   Penalty
§ 111.01 RECITALS.
   The recitals found in the ordinance from which this subchapter is derived
are found to be fact and are incorporated in the operative portion of this
subchapter by reference with the same full force and effect as though fully set
forth herein. Such findings are incorporated herein as an expression of the
intent of the Village Board in adopting this subchapter.
(Ord. 2020-07, passed 11-4-2019)
§ 111.02 PERMITTED FACILITIES.
   The Village Board adopts this subchapter allowing video gambling in the
following statutorily described facilities.
   (A)   LICENSED LARGE TRUCK STOP ESTABLISHMENT means a facility:
      (1)   At least a three-acre facility with a convenience store;
      (2)   With separate diesel islands for fueling commercial motor vehicles;
      (3)   Sells at retail more than 10,000 gallons of diesel or commercial
fuel per month; and
      (4)   With parking spaces for commercial motor vehicles.
   (B)   COMMERCIAL MOTOR VEHICLES has the same meaning as defined in § 18b-101
of the State Vehicle Code.
   (C)   The requirement of division (A)(3) above may be met by showing that
estimated future sales or past sales average at least 10,000 gallons per month.
(Ord. 2020-07, passed 11-4-2019; Ord. 2020-07-A, passed 9-8-2020)
§ 111.03 LICENSES AND FEES.
   There is hereby imposed upon each licensed truck stop establishment in the
village an annual fee of $25 per video gaming terminal located upon the
licensed premises. The terms VIDEO GAMING TERMINAL and LICENSED TRUCK STOP
ESTABLISHMENT shall have the same meanings as those set forth in the Video
Gaming Act, as now exists or is hereafter amended. Such license fee shall be
due and payable to the Village Clerk in January of each year, commencing with
January 2020.
(Ord. 2020-07, passed 11-4-2019)
§ 111.99 PENALTY.
   (A)   Any person violating any provision of this chapter for which no
specific penalty is prescribed shall be subject to §
10.99 of this code of ordinances.
   (B)   (1)   Any licensed truck stop establishment that fails to pay such fee
as described in §
111.03 during the month of January shall be subject to a fine for violation of
§§
111.01 through
111.03 in the amount of $100 plus court costs. Each day said license fee
remains unpaid following January 31 in any given year shall be deemed a
separate offense.
      (2)   There shall be penalties hereby adopted for violating the
provisions of §§
111.01 through
111.03, namely: any person, firm, or corporation found guilty of violating any
provision of §§
111.01 through
111.03 in the village shall be subject to the following penalties:
         (a)   A monetary fine up to $750;
         (b)   The requirement that the defendant perform up to 150 hours of
community service; or
         (c)   Imprisonment up to six months in penal institution other than a
penitentiary.
(Ord. 2020-07, passed 11-4-2019)
