GENERAL REGULATIONS
§ 152.001 DEFINITIONS.
   For the purpose of this chapter, the following definitions apply unless the
context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning.
   AFFIDAVIT. An oath in writing, sworn before and attested by an individual
who has the authority to administer an oath.
   APPLICANT. Any person making application for a license or permit.
   DEPENDENT MOBILE HOME. A mobile home which does not have toilet and bath or
shower facilities.
   IMMOBILIZED MOBILE HOME. A mobile home served by individual utilities,
resting on a permanent perimeter foundation which extends below the established
frost depth with the wheels, tongue, and hitch removed and the home secured in
compliance with the Mobile Home Tie-Down Act.
   INDEPENDENT MOBILE HOME. A mobile home which has a self-contained toilet and
bath or shower facilities.
   LICENSE. A license certificate issued by the village, allowing a person to
operate and maintain a mobile home park under the provisions of this chapter
and the rules and regulations issued hereunder.
   LICENSEE. Any person having a license or permit under this chapter.
   LOT SIZE. The minimum LOT SIZE shall be provided. However, the lot shall be
at least 75 feet wide and at least 100 feet deep. No mobile home shall be
located within 15 feet of any lot line, nor closer than 25 feet of an existing
building.
   MANUFACTURED/MODULAR HOME.
      (1)   A structure, transportable in one or more sections, which is 320 or
more square feet when erected on its site and designed to be used as a dwelling
unit with a permanent foundation when connected to the required utilities and
includes the plumbing, heating, air conditioning, and electrical systems
contained therein.
      (2)   Units composed of two or more separate components designed to be
joined into one integral unit.
      (3)   In addition, the term MANUFACTURED OR MODULAR HOME also includes
panelized, sectional, or modular units known as MANUFACTURED HOUSING UNITS,
which are regulated by the State Department of Public Health. These UNITS are
defined as a building assembly or system of building subassemblies, designed
for habitation as a dwelling for one or more persons, including the necessary
electrical, plumbing, heating, ventilating, and other service systems, which is
of closed or open construction and which is made for installation or assembly
and installation of the building site with a permanent foundation.
   MOBILE HOME.
      (1)   A structure designed for permanent habitation and so constructed as
to permit it from the place of its construction to the location, or subsequent
location, at which it is intended to be a permanent habitation and designed to
permit the occupancy thereof as a dwelling place for one or more persons. The
MOBILE HOME may consist of one or more sections.
      (2)   A type of manufactured housing built on and permanently affixed to
a steel chassis and possessing physical requirements as described and having a
label permanently affixed to the rear of each towable unit denoting compliance
with the “National Manufactured Home Construction and Safety Standards.”
      (3)   Housing designated and so constructed to be defined as a MOBILE
HOME subject to all regulations applicable thereto, whether or not wheels,
axles, hitch, or other appurtenances of mobility are removed and regardless of
the foundation provided.
      (4)   A dwelling unit with or without a permanent foundation when
connected to the required utilities and includes the plumbing, heating, air
conditioning, and electrical systems contained therein.
   MOBILE HOME PARK. A tract of land or two or more contiguous tracts of land
which contain sites with more independent mobile homes for permanent habitation
either free of charge or for revenue purposes, and shall include any building,
structure, vehicle, or enclosure used or intended for use as a part of the
equipment of such MOBILE HOME PARK. Separate ownership of contiguous tracts of
land shall not preclude the tracts of land from complying with this section as
a MOBILE HOME PARK if they are maintained and operated jointly. However, if
each proposed contiguous site for two mobile homes contains a minimum of 6,000
square feet with a 50-foot frontage, it will be exempt from complying with this
section. Neither an immobilized mobile home nor a motorized recreational
vehicle shall be construed as being a part of a MOBILE HOME PARK. A MOBILE HOME
PARK shall not be permitted within the village corporate limits.
   OWNER or OPERATOR. The licensee.
   PERMIT. A permit certificate issued by the village permitting the
construction, alteration, or reduction in number of spaces of a mobile home
park under the provisions of this subchapter and the rules and regulations
issued hereunder by the village.
   PERSON. Any individual, group of individuals, association, trust,
partnership, corporation, person doing business under an assumed name, county,
municipality, the state, or any political subdivision or department thereof, or
any other entity.
   REVOCATION. To declare invalid a permit or license issued to the applicant
or licensee by this village for an indefinite period of time.
   SITE. The lot on which the mobile home is harbored.
   SKIRTING. Used to conceal all underpinning, plumbing, and support piers, and
shall be applied no more than 30 days after occupancy.
   SPACE. Synonymous with SITE.
   SUSPENSION. To declare invalid a permit or license issued to the applicant
or licensee by this village, for a temporary period of time with an expectation
or resumption.
(Prior Code, § 23-1-1) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 152.002 ZONING COMPLIANCE.
   Mobile homes shall conform to zoning laws and requirements for lot size,
building size, and building location on lot along with all other regulations
and requirements established in the zoning ordinance of the village.
(Prior Code, § 23-1-2) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 152.003 DEPENDENT MOBILE HOMES PROHIBITED.
   No dependent mobile home shall be permitted to be located in the village. A
dependent mobile home is defined as one that does not have toilet, bath, or
shower facilities.
(Prior Code, § 23-1-3)
§ 152.004 MOBILE HOMES; REAL ESTATE TAX.
   All immobilized mobile homes located in the municipality and not in mobile
home parks shall be classified as REAL ESTATE. All persons owning, operating,
renting, or leasing a mobile home shall remove or cause to have removed the
wheels or any other transportation device from the mobile home. The owner or
lessor shall permanently affix said mobile home to the ground in a manner that
conforms to the definition of an immobilized mobile home in this chapter.
(Prior Code, § 23-1-4) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 152.005 SMOKE ALARMS.
   All mobile homes shall have smoke alarms in the vicinity of the furnace and/
or kitchen area and have two fire extinguishers in working order, one in each
end of the mobile home.
(Prior Code, § 23-1-5) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 152.006 TIE-DOWN REQUIREMENTS.
   All mobile homes shall have approved tie-downs.
(Prior Code, § 23-1-7) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 152.007 CONCRETE PAD.
   (A)   All mobile homes shall be placed on a mobile home pad constructed of
Portland cement concrete that shall be at least 12 inches below the freeze
line. In addition, all mobile home pads shall be at least ten feet wide by 60
feet in length, or mobile homes may be placed on solid concrete piers on a
solid concrete footing. Such piers and footings shall be of a size and kind
approved by the Village Board and shall be exactly as approved.
   (B)   Expandable units shall be provided with approved piers or their
equivalent at each corner of the unit.
(Prior Code, § 23-1-9) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 152.008 UTILITY SERVICE CONNECTION.
   No person shall become eligible for a municipal utility service connection
for a mobile home within the village corporate limits except upon proof of
special use permit.
(Prior Code, § 23-1-10)
§ 152.009 WATER SUPPLY AND DISTRIBUTION SYSTEM.
   An accessible, adequate, safe, and potable supply of water shall be provided
in each mobile home. Where a public supply of water is available at or near the
site, connection shall be made thereto and its supply used exclusively.
(Prior Code, § 23-1-11) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 152.010 SEWAGE DISPOSAL.
   Sewage disposal shall meet all village requirements in accordance with Title
V.
(Prior Code, § 23-1-13) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 152.011 FUEL STORAGE.
   (A)   All fuel storage tanks or cylinders shall be permanently installed and
securely fastened in place and shall not be located inside or beneath the
mobile home, or less than 15 feet from the mobile home exit/entrance.
   (B)   Fuel storage shall be permitted in tanks or containers mounted on an
incombustible frame at the rear of the mobile home. Fuel containers shall not
exceed 300 gallon capacity unless approved by the Village Board.
(Prior Code, § 23-1-15) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 152.012 NATURAL GAS OR CENTRAL BUTANE SYSTEM INSTALLATION.
   All gas piping installed below ground shall have a minimum earth cover of 18
inches. Gas mains shall not be installed under any mobile home.
(Prior Code, § 23-1-16) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 152.013 SYSTEM SHUT-OFF VALVE.
   A readily accessible and identified shut-off valve, controlling the flow of
fuel to the central fuel piping system, shall be installed near the point of
connection to the main fuel supply point.
(Prior Code, § 23-1-17) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 152.014 MOBILE HOME SHUT-OFF VALVE.
   Each mobile home shall have an approved fuel shut-off valve installed
upstream of the mobile fuel outlet and located on the outlet riser at a height
of not less than four inches above grade. Whenever the mobile home lot outlet
is not in use, the outlet shall be equipped with an approved cap or plug to
prevent accidental discharge of fuel.
(Prior Code, § 23-1-18) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 152.015 FUEL OIL DISTRIBUTION SYSTEMS.
   Piping installed below ground shall have a minimum earth cover of 18 inches
and all fuel lines shall be provided with a stopcock at the outlet of the fuel
container, and another stopcock just before the fuel line enters the mobile
home.
(Prior Code, § 23-1-19) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 152.016 OFF-STREET PARKING.
   Each mobile home owner shall provide for an off-street parking area of 400
square feet.
(Prior Code, § 23-1-20) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 152.017 ADDITIONAL MOBILE HOME REGULATIONS.
   (A)   Except as hereinafter provided, it shall be unlawful for any person,
firm, or corporation to maintain or locate any mobile home upon any plot or
parcel of land within the corporate limits of the village, except by a receipt
of a special use permit.
   (B)   Any mobile home situated within the village corporate limits upon the
effective date of this section shall, if in conformity to all sewer, water,
sanitation, health, building code, tie-down, or other ordinances or statutes,
be permitted to remain at its present location but may not be replaced by
another mobile home or moved to another location within the village corporate
limits, except in conformity with the provisions of this subchapter and the
zoning ordinance of the village.
   (C)   Special use permits will only be issued for single-family, owner-
occupied mobile homes except in the case of non-residential use in Districts B-
1, B-2, and M-1 (but shall require a special use permit). Exemptions to this
regulation shall require a variance.
   (D)   No mobile home which is more than seven years old may be placed within
the village corporate limits under any special use permit.
   (E)   The enlargement of livable space or the addition of a room in a mobile
home shall require a special use permit. The addition of a porch, sun deck,
patio, or similar addition shall be considered a permitted use.
(Prior Code, § 23-1-21) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 152.018 MOBILE HOME SKETCHES.
[https://export.amlegal.com/media/a0a6d9a3426d54295963d10b79448e3003dbd33c/
IMAGES/0-0-0-1454.png]
 
(Prior Code, § Figure 1)
MOBILE HOME PARKS
§ 152.030 TO REDUCE NUMBER OF LICENSED SITES.
   An application to reduce the number of sites shall be submitted to the
village no later than ten days prior to the proposed date of reduction. The
specific sites no longer required to be licensed, and either the method of
disconnecting the required utilities or a description of the method of
immobilizing the mobile homes shall be provided. If the reduction results in
less than two mobile homes remaining, the license shall be void if the
application is approved. No fee shall be required. The licensee shall be
responsible for ensuring that all utilities at vacated spaces are disconnected
or sealed, as prescribed by the village.
(Prior Code, § 23-2-1)
§ 152.031 TO REISSUE VOIDED, SUSPENDED, DENIED, OR REVOKED LICENSE.
   A mobile home park whose license has been voided, suspended, denied, or
revoked may be relicensed by submission of the application items required in
paragraphs (A), (B), (C), and (E) of this section and an application fee of
$50, which is non-refundable. Approval shall be issued if an inspection of the
park indicates compliance with this subchapter and the rules promulgated to
this subchapter.
(Prior Code, § 23-2-2)
§ 152.032 LOCAL GOVERNMENT REQUIREMENTS.
   (A)   A permit does not relieve the applicant from securing building permits
in the village or the county having a building code, or from complying with any
village or county zoning or other ordinance applicable thereto.
   (B)   Within ten days of receiving an application for a permit to construct
a new park or expand a licensed park, the village shall send a copy thereof, by
certified mail, to the County Clerk. Construction for which the village has
issued a permit shall not commence until the applicant has received any
required village or county zoning approvals. No license to operate and maintain
a mobile home park shall be issued upon the village’s being notified, within 60
days of the mailing of the application to the county, as provided in this
subchapter by a written certification from the village or County Zoning Board
or Commission that such park is in violation of any village or county zoning or
other ordinances and that such park was not in existence at the time of the
passage of the village or county zoning or other ordinances.
   (C)   Upon certification from such village or County Zoning Board that such
park has complied with the village or county zoning or other ordinances and
other requirements of this subchapter have been met, such license shall be
issued. Within ten days after such park has complied with the village or county
zoning ordinance, the village or County Zoning Board shall certify such
compliance to the village. Provided, fees charged by the village or county for
such permits shall not exceed the usual charge for the services provided by the
village or county in connection with such permits.
(Prior Code, § 23-2-3)
§ 152.033 PERMITS.
   Upon receipt of an application for a permit to construct a new mobile home
park, or an application for an original license to operate and maintain the
same, or an application for a permit to alter a licensed mobile home park, the
village shall, if the park is, or the proposed park will be, in conformity with
this subchapter and the rules and regulations adopted by the village pursuant
thereto, issue a permit to construct, a permit to alter, or an original
license, as the case may be. If the application for a permit to construct, a
permit to alter, or an original license is declined, the village shall give the
reasons therefor in writing to the applicant, and if the objections can be
corrected, the applicant may amend his or her application and re-submit for
approval. Permits shall be valid for one year from date of issue.
(Prior Code, § 23-2-4)
§ 152.034 LICENSES.
   (A)   Issuance. If a permit to construct or a permit to alter a park has
been issued, the applicant, upon completion thereof, shall notify the village.
The village shall then inspect the park and, if completed in accordance with
the approved plans, shall issue a license for the number of approved sites
after receipt of the required fee.
   (B)   Fees.
      (1)   In addition to the application fees provided for herein, the
licensee shall pay to the village, on or before March 31 of each year, an
annual license fee, which shall be $100 plus $3 for each mobile home space in
the park. Annual license fees submitted after April 30 shall be subject to a
$50 late fee. The licensee shall also complete and return a license renewal
application by March 31 of each year. The licensee shall pay to the village
within 30 days of receipt of notification from the village $6 for each
additional mobile home site added to his or her park under authority of a
written permit to alter the park as provided in § 23.27 of this subchapter.
      (2)   Payment for the additional mobile sites to be made an amended
license therefor obtained before any mobile homes are accommodated on the
additional mobile home spaces. The village shall issue an amended license to
cover such additional mobile home sites when they are to be occupied before the
end of the license year, for which an annual license has been previously
issued.
      (3)   An applicant for an original license to operate a new park
constructed under a permit issued by the village shall only be required to pay
one-fourth of the annual fee if such park begins operation after January 31 and
before May 1 of such licensing year, or one-half of the annual fee if such park
begins operation after October 31 and before February 1 of such licensing year
or three-fourths of the annual fee if such park begins operation after July 31
and before November 1 of such licensing year, but shall be required to pay the
entire annual fee if such park begins operation after April 30 and before
August 1 of such licensing year. Each license fee shall be paid to the village,
and any license fee or any part thereof, once paid to and accepted by the
village, shall not be refunded. The village shall deposit all funds received
under this chapter in the Village Depository.
(Prior Code, § 23-2-5)
§ 152.035 VIOLATION PROCEEDINGS.
   Any license granted hereunder shall be subject to revocation or suspension
by the village. However, the village shall first serve or cause to be served
upon the licensee a written notice in which shall be specified the way or ways
in which such licensee has failed to comply with the statute, or any rules or
regulations promulgated by the village pertaining thereto. The notice shall
require the licensee to remove or abate such nuisance, unsanitary, or
objectionable condition, specified in such notice, within five days or within a
longer period of time as may be allowed by the village. If the licensee fails
to comply with the terms and conditions of the notice, within the time
specified or such extended period of time, the village may revoke or suspend
such license.
(Prior Code, § 23-2-6)
§ 152.036 TRANSFER OF LICENSE.
   All licenses issued under this chapter shall be transferable only with the
written consent of the village; provided, however, that the village may not
withhold such consent where the provisions of this subchapter have been met.
The new licensee shall provide to the village the information required in
paragraphs (A), (C), and (E) of § 23.27.
(Prior Code, § 23-2-7)
§ 152.037 DISPLAY OF LICENSE AND PERMITS.
   No person, firm, or corporation shall construct a mobile home park without
first obtaining a permit to do so. All permits to construct, all licenses to
operate, and all permits to make alterations therein shall be prominently
displayed in the park office.
(Prior Code, § 23-2-8) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 152.038 MANAGEMENT OF MOBILE HOME PARK.
   Every park shall be managed by a responsible individual whose name, address,
and telephone number shall be on file at all times with the village and whose
duty it shall be to maintain the park, its facilities, and equipment in a
clean, orderly, and sanitary condition, and shall be responsible, with the
licensee, for any violation of the provisions of this code.
(Prior Code, § 23-2-9) Penalty, see §
10.99
DESIGN AND CONSTRUCTION REQUIREMENTS
§ 152.050 PLAN DOCUMENT.
   In order to obtain a permit to construct or an original license to operate a
mobile home park, the applicant shall file with the village a written
application and plan documents, and such plan documents shall be prepared by a
registered engineer or architect licensed to practice in the state, with
registration seal affixed. Two copies of the plan document shall accompany the
application filed with the village to obtain a permit to construct or alter a
mobile home park or an original license to operate a mobile home park, not
previously licensed by the Department. These plans shall include, but not be
limited to, the design and construction criteria set forth herein.
(Prior Code, § 23-2-10)
§ 152.051 LOCATION.
   (A)   Sites selected for mobile home development shall be well drained and
free from topographical or geological hindrances and from other conditions
unfavorable to a proper residential environment. The mobile home development
shall not be located near swamps, marshes, or other breeding places of insects,
rats, and mice. When a good natural drainage is not available, storm drainage
shall be provided, and such drainage shall not endanger any water supply or
surface watercourse.
   (B)   The village may conduct a site survey to ascertain that the proposed
location complies with the requirements of division (A) above.
(Prior Code, § 23-2-11) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 152.052 ROADWAYS AND PARKING.
   (A)   All streets and driveways in every park shall be maintained in a
passable and reasonably dust-proof condition at all times.
   (B)   All streets and driveways in parks constructed shall have a minimum
road width of 26 feet.
   (C)   All roadways in mobile home parks shall provide convenient vehicular
traffic flow in accordance with one of the following specifications.
 
Road Width Parking
26 ft.     No parking on roadway
30 ft.     Parking one side of street
36 ft.     Parking two sides of street
Notes to table:
Parking restrictions do not apply whenever traffic flow is one-way.
 
   (D)   Sidewalks and walkways in the mobile home park, where provided, shall
be a minimum of three and one-half feet in width, with no minimum width
requirement for sidewalks in each individual lot. No portion of a mobile home
shall block, in any way, the pedestrian traffic on the walkways.
   (E)   All mobile home spaces shall be equipped with one off-street parking
space of at least 15 feet wide and 20 feet deep.
(Prior Code, § 23-2-12) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 152.053 MOBILE HOME SITES AND SPACING.
   (A)   Each site on which each mobile home is accommodated shall have a
minimum area of 2,500 square feet.
   (B)   (1)   No mobile home shall be parked closer than five feet to the side
lot lines of a park, or closer than ten feet to a public street, alley, or
building. Each individual site shall abut or face on a private or public
street.
      (2)   All streets shall have unobstructed access to a public street.
There shall be an open space of at least ten feet adjacent to the sides of
every mobile home and at least five feet adjacent to the ends of every mobile
home.
   (C)   All mobile home sites, irrespective of shape, shall have a minimum
frontage of 50 linear feet, and comply with the minimum area requirement as
stated in division (A) above.
   (D)   Concrete pads, at least six inches thick, shall be provided for each
lot. A perimeter footing of at least 24 inches shall be provided for each pad.
The area of the concrete pad shall equal the square footage of the mobile home.
   (E)   Anchors and tie-downs for mobile homes shall be installed at the
corners of each pad or as otherwise deemed necessary for protection against
high winds. Each anchor should be capable of withstanding a vertical tension
force of 4,800 pounds.
(Prior Code, § 23-2-13) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 152.054 POTABLE WATER SUPPLY.
   An adequate supply of water of safe, sanitary quality approved by the
village shall be furnished at each pad. Each site shall be provided with a cold
water tap located in accordance per regulations of the Department of Public
Health and the village.
(Prior Code, § 23-2-14) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 152.055 DISTRIBUTION SYSTEM.
   (A)   All plumbing shall be installed in accordance with the State Plumbing
Code.
   (B)   The diameter of the pipe required shall be no less than four inches in
all areas of the park. The distribution system shall be looped whenever
possible, and dead-end mains shall be equipped with flush hydrants or
equivalent.
   (C)   The laying of the water main, in relation to the location of the sewer
main, shall be in accordance with the following.
      (1)   On new installation of all water mains and sewer mains shall not be
less than ten feet apart horizontally and shall be separated by undisturbed or
compacted earth. Should conditions prevail which would prevent a lateral
separation of ten feet, the water service pipe may be placed in the same trench
as the sewer service pipe, provided the following conditions are met.
         (a)   The bottom of the water service pipe at all points shall be at
least 18 inches above the top of the sewer line.
         (b)   The water service pipe shall be placed on a solid shelf
excavated at one side of the common trench.
         (c)   The number of joints in the water and sewer service pipe shall
be kept at a minimum.
      (2)   Water and sewer lines shall not cross except where such crossings
cannot be reasonably avoided. At necessary crossings, the water line shall be
kept at least 18 inches above the top of the sewer, which vertical separation
shall be maintained at least ten feet from each side of the crossings or the
sewer shall be constructed of cast iron pipe, type K copper, or DWV plastic
pipe (Schedule 40) with water-tight joints for a distance of ten feet from each
side of the water line. All crossings shall be made at right angles and the
water and sewer pipe lengths shall be centered such that the joints are as
remote as possible from the crossing. The materials in joint construction for
the water and sewer service lines shall be in accordance with §§ 10.10.1 and
11.2.2 of the State Plumbing Code.
      (3)   On new installations, all water service connection lines and sewer
connections shall not be less than ten feet apart horizontally and shall be
separated by undisturbed or compacted earth.
   (D)   A water service connection shall not be less than three-fourths of an
inch inside diameter and shall not serve more than one mobile home at any time.
   (E)   All water risers shall be at least three-fourths of an inch in
diameter and terminate at least four inches above finished ground level.
   (F)   On new installations, water supply outlets at each mobile home shall
be separated not less than ten feet horizontally from the sewer outlet.
   (G)   All corporation stops and valve cocks shall be approved by the
village. Combination stop and waste valves and cocks shall not be installed in
an underground service pipe.
(Prior Code, § 23-2-15) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 152.056 COST OF WATER CONNECTION.
   The cost of a water connection shall be in accordance with the regulations
established in Title V.
(Prior Code, § 23-2-16) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 152.057 SEWERAGE DISPOSAL SYSTEM.
   (A)   There shall be no discharge of raw or partially treated sewage or
waste water onto the surface of the ground, nor shall there be any escape of
odors from the drainage systems. All sewerage systems serving mobile home parks
shall be designed and operated in accordance with good sanitation practices and
shall meet the requirements of the State Department of Public Health. Plans for
new installations shall be submitted to the Department of Public Health for
review and approval as part of the total proposed park plan. The design of
sewerage system and sewerage treatment facility for a mobile home park shall be
based on the maximum number of mobile home spaces and designed and constructed
on the basis of 250 gallons per space per day. When sewerage treatment
facilities are proposed with an above-ground discharge or surface discharge,
additional plans may be required by the Environmental Protection Agency. All
sewerage shall be into a private system which includes a sanitary means of
disposal, the operation of which creates neither a nuisance or a menace to
health. All liquid waste from each mobile home shall discharge into an approved
sewerage disposal system.
   (B)   Each site shall be provided with a sewer connection for the combined
liquid waste outlet or outlets of each mobile home. It shall be the duty of the
owner or operator of said park to provide an approved type of water- and odor-
tight connection from the mobile home water drainage to the sewer connection,
and it shall be the duty of the owner or operator to make such connection and
keep all occupied mobile homes connected to the sewer while located in the
park. Sewer connections in unoccupied sites shall be so closed that they will
emit no odors or cause a breeding place for flies. No water or waste shall be
allowed to fall on the ground from a mobile home. At all sewer connections, the
sewer riser shall extend four inches above the ground.
   (C)   Septic tank and subsurface seepage fields may be used for mobile home
parks provided the system is of proper design. The design should be based upon
the criteria of U.S. Department of Health, Education, and Welfare “Public
Health Service Bulletin Number 526, Manual of Septic Tank Practice.” Plans and
specifications for subsurface disposal facilities shall provide adequate
percolation data. A minimum of six test holes, at various locations throughout
the seepage field area are required. The ground water table, the size of septic
tanks and seepage fields, contours, elevations, slopes, and the like, must be
shown on the plans. Septic tanks and subsurface seepage tile shall be separated
from wells by the minimum distances specified in § 23.39, Table II, and shall
not be less than 50 feet from any lake, stream, or open ditch. No subsurface
disposal system shall have a septic tank storage capacity of less than 750
gallons, nor a subsurface tile field less than 250 square feet of absorption
area, with no trench width exceeding three feet. The effective absorption area
is to be considered as the area of the trench bottom.
   (D)   New construction and alterations of individual sewage disposal systems
shall be inspected by the design engineer or an authorized representative of
this village prior to being back-filled.
(Prior Code, § 23-2-17)
§ 152.058 SEWAGE COLLECTION SYSTEM.
   (A)   In new installations, sanitary sewers shall be separated by ten feet
horizontally from water supply lines wherever possible throughout their length.
If sewer lines cross water lines, the installation must meet the requirements
specified under § 23.40(B).
   (B)   The minimum design and slope of new sewer installations shall be
determined in accordance with the following:
 
Minimum Size and Slope of Sewers*
No. of Spaces Sewer Inside Diameter  Slope per 100 feet  Uses
              (In.)                  (In.)
1 to 125      6                      9                   Laterals and mains
More than 125 8                      6                   Mains
Notes to table:
*   Exclusive of laterals serving individual mobile homes.
 
   (C)   On new installations, manholes shall be provided at every change in
direction or grade, at the upper end of every main sewer line, at every
junction of two or more branch sewers, and at intervals of not more than 400
feet. Cleanouts extending to grade may be used instead of manholes on sewer
lines no greater than eight inches in diameter, and shall be at intervals of
not more than 100 feet.
(Prior Code, § 23-2-18) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 152.059 SOLID WASTE DISPOSAL.
   (A)   A sufficient number of adequate fly-proof and water-tight containers
shall be supplied for the storage of garbage.
   (B)   Garbage containers shall be emptied at least once a week and shall not
be filled to overflowing, or allowed to become foul smelling or a breeding
place for insects. Garbage and rubbish shall be disposed of in a manner which
creates neither a nuisance nor a menace to health and which is approved by the
village. Individual refuse containers shall be located at each space or bulk
containers shall be located within 150 feet from any mobile home. All
containers shall be stored at least eight inches off the ground surface or on
an impervious slab or other installations approved by the village, all refuse,
which includes, garbage, rubbish, and tin cans shall be stored in a durable,
rust resistant, non-absorbent, watertight, rodent-proof container having a
tight fitting lid which shall be maintained in a sanitary condition and in good
repair at all times. The minimum capacity for refuse containers shall be a
ratio of 40 gallons per mobile home per week or a ratio of 40 gallons per
mobile home per week when a centralized collection system is utilized.
   (C)   Paper and plastic bags designed specifically for solid waste, may be
used on occasion as a supplement to basic storage containers provided that they
are properly closed, attached to a holder, properly stored above ground to
prevent scattering by animal or human, and no evidence of rodent activity is
observed.
   (D)   The collection of all solid waste shall be performed by the Village
Garbage Contractor.
(Prior Code, § 23-2-19) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 152.060 FIRE PROTECTION.
   Mobile homes in mobile home parks shall be equipped with fire extinguishers
in working order, one in each end of the mobile home.
(Prior Code, § 23-2-20) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 152.061 EXTERIOR LIGHTING.
   Adequate lighting shall be provided for all streets, walkways, buildings,
and other facilities subject to night-time use. There shall be an average
illumination level of at least six-tenths foot candle and a minimum
illumination level of three-tenths foot candle maintained on all streets. To
achieve this level of illumination, the village recommends the use of 175-watt
mercury-vapor lamp, or a 600-watt tungsten lamp, at an elevation of 25 feet,
every 250 feet. Individual electric or gas yard lights, having an average
equivalent illumination of a 40-watt electric light bulb per space will be
acceptable in lieu of a central lighting system.
(Prior Code, § 23-2-21) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 152.062 VECTOR CONTROL.
   (A)   Adequate insect and rodent control measures shall be employed by the
mobile home park owner. All buildings shall be fly and rodent proof, and rodent
harborages shall not be permitted to exist in the park or pathways.
   (B)   The mobile home park owner shall eliminate any insect, rat, or mice
problem in the park which is a potential health hazard.
(Prior Code, § 23-2-22) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 152.063 ELECTRICAL DISTRIBUTION.
   (A)   Underground electrical lines shall be placed at least 18 inches below
the ground, surface and at least one foot radial distance from water, sewer,
gas, or communication lines. If overhead power lines are installed, they shall
be at least 18 feet above streets or roadways. A minimum horizontal clearance
of at least three feet shall be provided between overhead lines and any
structure.
   (B)   The electrical cable supplying electrical service from the weather-
proof receptacle to the mobile home must be buried six inches below ground
level from the receptacle to a point directly below the entrance to the mobile
home or be suspended and adequately supported at least seven feet above ground
level from a point vertical to the receptacle to the mobile home.
   (C)   No connected electrical extension cord shall lie on the ground or be
suspended less than seven feet from the ground above sidewalks or pathways. All
electrical wiring, equipment, and appurtenances shall be installed and
maintained in accordance with applicable local government codes and
regulations. A properly grounded, weather-proof receptacle shall be provided
for each mobile home site.
(Prior Code, § 23-2-23) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 152.064 FUEL SUPPLY AND STORAGE.
   All handling and storage of natural gas, liquefied petroleum gas (LPG), fuel
oil, or other flammable liquid or gases should be installed and maintained in
accordance with applicable state and local government codes and regulations.
The State Department of Law Enforcement (Division of Fire Prevention) is the
regulatory state agency for safe fuel storage and handling systems and the
applicable regulations are the National Fire Protection Association Standards,
NFPA-31 “Installation of Oil Burning Equipment-1968,” NFPA-54, “Installation of
Gas Appliances and Gas Piping-1969,” and NFPA-58, “Storage and Handling of
Liquefied Petroleum Gases 1969.” No LPG or fuel oil container shall be placed
inside or beneath any mobile home, storage cabinet, carport, or any other
structure unless such arrangement is approved by the appropriate authority.
Containers of fuel shall be at least five feet from any mobile home door or
exits, and placed on stands constructed of a noncombustible material.
(Prior Code, § 23-2-24) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 152.065 SWIMMING POOLS AND BEACHES.
   Swimming pools and beaches, if provided, shall be constructed and operated
in accordance with applicable state statute and all rules and regulations
adopted pursuant thereto. Separate plans and specifications are to be submitted
to this village for approval prior to construction.
(Prior Code, § 23-2-25) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 152.066 SERVICE BUILDINGS.
   (A)   Plans and specifications for service buildings, containing community
kitchens, dining rooms, laundries, lavatory and toilet facilities, or other
facilities are subject to review by the village.
   (B)   All plumbing within a service building shall comply with the State
Plumbing Code. All electrical and heating installations shall be in accordance
with existing county building ordinances.
   (C)   The facilities and equipment of all service buildings shall be
maintained in a sanitary condition and kept in good repair, subject to
inspection by the village.
(Prior Code, § 23-2-26) Penalty, see §
10.99
MOBILE HOME PARK MAINTENANCE AND OPERATION REGULATIONS
§ 152.080 NOTIFICATION OF RULES AND REGULATIONS BY PARK OWNER.
   (A)   The mobile home park owner shall notify the mobile home residents of
all applicable provisions of the Mobile Home Park Law and rules and regulations
for mobile home parks and inform them of their duties and responsibilities
required by the village.
   (B)   The mobile home park owner shall draft and adopt a separate set of
rules and regulations governing the maintenance of the mobile home park to keep
its facilities and equipment in good repair and in clean and sanitary
condition. Under these rules and regulations, the mobile home park owner shall
identify the responsibilities of the management to the mobile home owner and
shall further identify the responsibilities of the resident in the mobile home
park.
   (C)   The local rules and regulations established by the mobile home park
owner shall contain, but not be limited to, the control of pets, the storage of
refuse and garbage, the design and construction of auxiliary structures, the
control of abandoned automobiles, the control of the growth of weeds and grass,
control of insects, rats, and mice and all other rules and regulations
necessary to maintain the mobile home park, its facilities, and equipment in
good repair and in a clean and sanitary condition.
   (D)   The mobile home park resident shall be informed of the local rules and
regulations governing the maintenance and operation of the mobile home park.
   (E)   The local rules and regulations, established by the mobile home park
owner, shall not relieve the mobile home park owner or caretaker of compliance
with the State Mobile Home Park Law or “Rules and Regulations for State Mobile
Home Parks.”
(Prior Code, § 23-2-30) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 152.081 REGISTRATION.
   (A)   Each mobile home park shall be provided with a custodian’s office
where each mobile home entering such park shall be assigned to a site, given a
copy of the park rules, and registered according to the prescribed form. Such
registration shall include the name and address of the owner and every occupant
of such mobile home and the square feet of the floor space contained in such
mobile home. Such registration shall also include the license number of the
mobile home and of the towing vehicle, if there be any, and the state issuing
such licenses. The register shall be signed by the owner or operator of the
mobile home.
   (B)   Any person furnishing misinformation for purposes of registration
shall be deemed guilty of a misdemeanor and punishable under the general
statutes for such offense.
   (C)   The registration records shall be neatly and securely maintained, and
no registration records shall be destroyed until six years have elapsed
following the date of registration. The register shall be available at all
times for inspection by all law enforcement officers and by the village.
(Prior Code, § 23-2-31) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 152.082 COMMUNICABLE OR CONTAGIOUS DISEASE.
   The mobile home park owner or caretaker shall notify the village immediately
of any suspected communicable or contagious disease within the mobile home
park.
(Prior Code, § 23-2-32) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 152.083 INSPECTION DOOR REQUIRED.
   An inspection door for use by the village representative or licensee that is
easily removable, a sliding type or hinge type, located near the sewer riser,
shall be provided on all mobile home skirting and shall be a minimum of 24
inches in width.
(Prior Code, § 23-2-33) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 152.084 FENCING.
   Perimeter fencing of individual sites, where permitted by the park owner,
shall not exceed three one-half feet in height.
(Prior Code, § 23-2-34) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 152.085 ABANDONED VEHICLES AND THE LIKE.
   Any abandoned automobile or piece of equipment having the appearance of
being abandoned shall be removed from the park.
(Prior Code, § 23-2-35)
§ 152.086 BUILDING MATERIALS.
   Lumber or similar building materials shall be stacked in a neat and orderly
manner at least six inches above the ground surface.
(Prior Code, § 23-2-36) Penalty, see §
10.99

§ 153.01 DEFINITIONS.
   For the purpose of this chapter, the following definitions apply unless the
context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning.
   EASEMENT. A quantity or area of land set aside or designated for, or over,
under, along, or across which, a liberty, privilege, or advantage of land,
existing distinct from the ownership of the land or from a fee simple interest
in the land, is granted to the general public, some part of the general public,
or some particular person.
   OWNER. Includes the plural as well as the singular and means either a
natural person, firm, association, partnership, private corporation, public or
quasi-public corporation, or any combination of the foregoing.
   PLAT. A map of a land subdivision containing the information hereinafter
specified and complying with the following requirements.
      (1)   It shall meet the requirements of the Plat Act, 765 ILCS 205/1 et
seq., as from time to time amended, which as public record, is, by virtue of §
1-3-1 of the State Municipal Code, is incorporated herein by record.
      (2)   It shall have been prepared by, pursuant to a survey made by, a
land surveyor registered in and by the state.
      (3)   It shall have particularly described and set forth therein all
public streets, alleys, ways for public service facilities, ways for utility
services and community antenna televisions systems, parks, playgrounds, school
grounds, or other public grounds, and all the tracts, parcels, lots, or blocks,
and numbering all such lots, blocks, or parcels by progressive numbers, giving
their precise dimensions.
      (4)   It shall show all angular and linear data along the exterior
boundaries of a tract of land divided or subdivided.
      (5)   It shall show the names of all public streets and the width,
course, and extent of all public streets, alleys, and ways for public service
facilities.
      (6)   It shall make reference to known and permanent monuments from which
future survey may be made, which monuments shall have been set in such manner
that they will not be moved by frost, and good and sufficient monuments marking
the external boundaries of the tract to be divided or subdivided must be
designated upon the plat at the points where they may be found, which monuments
must be placed at all corners, at each end of all curves at the point where a
curve changes its radius, and at all angle points in any line and at all angle
points along a meander line, the points to be not less than 20 feet back from
the normal water elevation of a lake or from the bank of a stream, except that
when such corners or points fall within a street or a proposed future street
the monuments may be placed in the right-of-way line of a street.
      (7)   It shall show all internal boundaries, comers and points to be
monumented in the field by lot monuments as hereinabove defined, of which
monuments two must be of stone or reinforced concrete and must be set at the
opposite extremities of the property platted, placed at all block comers, at
each end of the curves, at the points where a curve changes its radius, and at
all angle points in a line, and it shall also show each lot to be monumented in
the field with two or more monuments.
      (8)   It shall show the proposed name of the subdivision, the location of
the subdivision by section, township, and range, the names and addresses of the
owner and the designer of the subdivision, and shall be at a scale of 100 feet
to the inch with a designated north point.
      (9)   It shall show each lot area, lot depth, lot width, and front yard,
rear yard, and side yard setback requirements, if any, to be in accordance with
the existing zoning laws and ordinances of the village.
      (10)   It shall show and provide for easements for public utilities,
whether in the form of alleyways or otherwise.
      (11)   It shall show or otherwise have appended thereto a typical street
cross-section.
      (12)   It shall have been properly certified by a land surveyor
registered in and by the state and acknowledged by the owner.
      (13)   It shall show proposed location of any pipelines for water,
natural gas, and sewer pipelines to be constructed pursuant to a subdivision
agreement and the point at which main construction is proposed to be connected
to the village’s systems.
   STREET. The entire width between property lines of every way or place of
whatever nature when any part thereof is opened to the use of the public as a
matter of right for the purpose of vehicular or pedestrian traffic, including
any public or private way which affords access by pedestrians and vehicles to
abutting property.
   SUBDIVISION. The division of a lot, tract, or parcel of land as determined
by the dimensions and configuration on October 1, 1973, into two or more parts,
any of which is less than five acres and which involves, or includes, any new
street or easement of access.
   SUBDIVISION AGREEMENT. A written memorandum of agreement between the owner
and the village providing for the setting forth the responsibilities and
obligations of each party as to the performance and expense of construction,
installation, ownership, and maintenance of pipelines for the distribution of
water and natural gas and the collection of sewage from structures and
buildings which may be constructed on the land in the plat, and also providing
for any other matters pertaining to subdivision control to which the parties
may agree and which are riot inconsistent with or contrary to any provision or
requirement in the Plat Act.
   VILLAGE. The Village of Goreville, Johnson County, Illinois, a municipal
corporation.
(Ord. 2010-2, passed 7-20-2009) Penalty, see §
153.99
§ 153.02 FINAL APPROVAL OF PLAT REQUIRED.
   It shall be unlawful for any person do to any of the following until a plat
has been granted final approval certified, and recorded in the office of the
Recorder of Deeds of the county:
   (A)   Make any subdivision or lay out any street, easement of access, or
other public space;
   (B)   Make any plat of any subdivision and record the same in the Recorder’s
office of the county;
   (C)   Offer for sale, contract for sale, sell, or lease for any time
exceeding five years, any lot, tract, or parcel, or block of land within any
subdivision; or
   (D)   Make any improvements, such as water supply, drainage sewerage, sewage
disposal, gas services, electric service of lighting, or grating, paving, or
surfacing, or any street or other easement of access within any subdivision.
(Ord. 2010-2, passed 7-20-2009) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 153.03 SUBMISSION OF PROPOSAL.
   Any person desiring to make a subdivision may apply to the Village Board by
submitting in triplicate to the office of the Village Clerk:
   (A)   The proposed plat;
   (B)   Documents demonstrating compliance with the requirements of §
153.04(H) through (L);
   (C)   The owner’s written and express promise and undertaking to construct
and complete, at the owner’s expense, the streets shown on the plat within 12
months after preliminary approval of the plat, in accordance with the typical
section attached to the ordinance from which this chapter is derived as
Appendix A; and
   (D)   The owner’s written proposal regarding the location, construction, and
the bearing of and payment for the expense of installation or pipelines for the
expense of installation of pipelines for the distribution of water and natural
gas and collection of sewage with the subdivision, and statement of being
ready, willing, and able to enter into, a subdivision agreement as a condition
of the village’s approving the proposed plat.
(Ord. 2010-2, passed 7-20-2009)
§ 153.04 REQUIREMENTS FOR APPROVAL.
   The Village Board may consider and approve a proposed plat of a subdivision
only upon evidence that the proposal meets the following standards and
requirements hereby established for subdivision regulation and control:
   (A)   The proposed plat constitutes a plat as herein defined, and is
submitted in accordance with §
153.03;
   (B)   All taxes and assessments on the property platted shall have been
paid;
   (C)   The village’s zoning ordinance, if any, shall be complied with, or the
owner’s proposed declaration of restrictions, or other covenants to run with
the land upon sale thereof, if any, be provided, which declaration of
restrictions, if any, shall provide that the lot or lots contained in such
subdivision are subject, at a minimum, to the zoning ordinance of the village;
   (D)   A proposed form on the plat for an effective dedication of all
streets, easements, and other public spaces to be dedicated for as provided in
and by the plat, to the village and/or the general public, whichever is
appropriate;
   (E)   There shall be submitted, simultaneously with the plat, a study or
studies which shall show topographically and by profile the elevation of the
land prior to the commencement of any change in elevations a part of any phase
of subdividing, and additionally, if it is contemplated that such elevations or
the flow or surface water from such land, will be changed as a result of any
portion of such subdivision development, then such study of studies separate
from, but of the subsidiary study or studies separate from, but of the same
scale and. size as the subdivision plat, and shall be prepared in such a manner
as will permit the topographical study or studies to be used as overlays to the
subdivision plat;
   (F)   The plat shall have on its face the signed statement of a registered
professional engineer and the owner of the land, to the effect that to the best
of their knowledge and belief, the drainage of surface waters will not be
changed by the construction of such subdivision or any part thereof, or, that
if such surface water drainage will be changed, reasonable provisions has been
made for collection and diversion of such surface waters into public areas, or
drains which the subdivider has a right to use, and that such surface waters
will be planned for in accordance with generally accepted engineering practices
so as to reduce the likelihood of damage to the adjoining property because of
the construction of the subdivision;
   (G)   The plat shall have been approved in writing:
      (1)   By the State Department of Transportation with respect to roadway
access where such access is to a state highway;
      (2)   By the relevant local highway authority with respect to all other
roadway access; and
      (3)   By the Local Health Department, if one exists, with respect to
sewage disposal systems if any part of the platted land will not be served by a
public sewer system.
   (H)   The owner holds merchantable fee simple title to the real property
constituting the land described in the plat;
   (I)   The owner has completed construction of the streets, in accordance
with the minimum standards and requirements set forth in Appendix A of the
ordinance from which this chapter is derived;
   (J)   In the event that the owner is required, pursuant to a subdivision
agreement, to construct and install pipelines for the water and sewer, the
rules, regulations, and standards by and of the Society of Professional
Engineers, as set forth in its “Standard Specifications for Water and Sewer
Main Construction in Illinois,” have been complied with;
   (K)   In the event that either the streets required hereunder or pipeline
for water, sewage, or natural gas as required under any subdivision agreement
has not been constructed or construction has not been fully completed or paid
for, either within the time the plat is presented for final approval or within
the time permitted in any subdivision agreement, then the owner shall furnish
and provide to the village a bond or other sufficient security guaranteeing the
performance and payment of the construction or completion of construction of
such improvements in the amount of a duly licensed civil engineer’s estimate of
the full cost of constructing same, which bond shall be conditioned upon such
improvements in the amount of duly licensed engineer’s estimate of the full
cost of constructing same, which bond shall be conditioned upon the owner’s
construction and installation at owner’s expense, of all the improvements
described in said plat, and shall contain the owner’s agreement to maintain
such improvements constructed for a period of one year from the date of
completion thereof, which bond shall also save the village harmless from all
loss, cost, or damage, by reason of the owner’s failure to complete said work
or maintain said improvements for such period of time; and
   (L)   The plat is in all other respects in accordance with any and all other
laws, ordinances, regulations and rules of the United States of America and the
state, and all applicable agencies of the government of each, and of the
village, which may from time to time, apply to or regulate any aspect of the
subdivision of land for whatever purpose.
(Ord. 2010-2, passed 7-20-2009)
§ 153.05 PRELIMINARY APPROVAL.
   (A)   Upon the owner’s satisfaction of all of the requirements of §
153.04, except the construction and installation or completion of the
construction and installation of any streets required by this chapter or any
pipelines for water, sewage, or natural gas required by the subdivision
agreement, the Village Board may by resolution grant preliminary approval to
the proposed plat, with final approval and certification under §
153.06 subject to the owner’s completion of construction and installation of
said streets, pipelines, or other required by the subdivision agreement.
   (B)   A written resolution granting preliminary approval is binding on the
village and may be relied upon by the owner for the purpose of expending funds
for completion of the requirements, but shall not be endorsed on the plat.
   (C)   Preliminary approval does not constitute certification or approval and
does not authorize recording of the plat.
(Ord. 2010-2, passed 7-20-2009)
§ 153.06 FINAL APPROVAL, CERTIFICATION, AND RECORDING.
   (A)   Proof of the owner’s completion of the construction and installation
of the streets and pipelines, if any, required, and the sufficiency of any
provisions for diversion of surface waters, shall take the form of a
certification by the village’s consulting engineers that the standards of
construction herein required have been compiled with (hereinafter, “engineering
approval”). The cost and expense of engineering approval shall be borne by the
owner and paid directly to the village’s consulting engineers upon the
village’s notifying the owner of the amount thereof.
   (B)   After preliminary approval, and upon engineering approval, the Village
Board, by written resolution, shall grant final approval of the plat and
authorize the Mayor to certify final approval thereon, attested to by the
Village Clerk.
   (C)   A plat certified as provided in division (B) above shall be recorded
in the office of the Recorder of Deeds of the county.
   (D)   No plat shall be valid or entitled to recording until it shall have
been finally approved and certified as provided in this chapter.
   (E)   Any subdivision agreement shall also be recorded as a part of the same
document constituting the certified plat.
(Ord. 2010-2, passed 7-20-2009)
§ 153.07 ENFORCEMENT.
   (A)   Inasmuch as the enforcement of the regulations and controls herein
provided for is essential for the effectuation of the general plan of
development hereby contemplated, it is hereby declared that any violation of
any provisions of this chapter cannot be adequately compensated for by recovery
of damages and that there is no adequate remedy at law for any breach or any
violation of any provisions of this chapter, so that the village, any aggrieved
party, or any future owner of any lot, may require and shall be entitled to
equitable relief by injunction to restrain any violation of this chapter, in
addition to any other remedies provided by law.
   (B)   Each violation of this chapter is hereby declared to be and
constitutes a nuisance and every remedy allowed by law or equity against a
nuisance, either public or private, shall be applicable hereto, and such remedy
shall be deemed cumulative, not exclusive, and not in lieu of any other remedy.
(Ord. 2010-2, passed 7-20-2009)
§ 153.08 NAME, INCORPORATED RECORDS, AND PUBLICATION.
   (A)   This chapter shall be known and may be cited as “The Village of
Goreville Subdivision Control Ordinance.”
   (B)   This chapter shall be printed in book or pamphlet form, published by
authority of the village, and such book or pamphlet shall be prima facie
evidence of the contents, passage, and legal publication of this chapter as of
the dates hereinafter mentioned, and all courts and administrative tribunals,
and this chapter shall be in full force and effect from and after its passage,
approval, and publication in the manner provided by law.
   (C)   The chapter shall be recorded in the office of the Recorder of Deeds
for the county, for the purpose of aiding in determination of the sufficiency
of legal descriptions of lots platted hereunder, the recordability of
instruments of conveyance of those lots, and the legal sufficiency of plats
recorded pursuant to this chapter.
(Ord. 2010-2, passed 7-20-2009)
§ 153.99 PENALTY.
   It is unlawful for any person to commit any act prohibited by this chapter
or to fail to comply with any requirement hereof, and any person violating any
provisions of this chapter shall be fined in an amount not less than $100 and
not to exceed $1,000.
(Ord. 2010-2, passed 7-20-2009)
